Highlights at Corn Creek included a lengthy experience with an incredibly well seen and heard male Rose-breasted Grosbeak (first called out by Gerry Hawkins) plus a seen and heard singing Bell's Vireo (first called out by Bob Barnes) and at least 50 Western Tanagers.  New Nevada birds for this final day: Sharp-shinned Hawk (Gerry Hawkins only), Sora (Paul Fox only), definitive Anna's Hummingbird, Rose-breasted Grosbeak, and Hooded Oriole (Bob Barnes only). This Corn Creek stop was the start of the 8th and final full day of birding for this southern Nevada birding trip to Clark County Las Vegas area and Lincoln County, Nevada birding sites. Singing. Fast, harsh jumbled song ending on up note, then repeated ending on descending note. Very familiar with this song from Arizona. As was typical there, the birds stayed in dense brush and would not respond to pishing.----As I heard the first bird at the beginning of the boardwalk, a photographer approached returning to the parking lot. He saw my binoculars and asked, "Birding?" to which I replied in the affirmative. As he continued by, he tossed off the question, "These Bell's Vireos I'm hearing?" I confirmed that.----Early return.
